```text
id: 091-range-reversal-rev
move: append `.rev()` to a parenthesized range — `(1..4).rev()` — to make a `for` loop walk the range in descending order; concretely the working probe `fn main() { for number in (1..4).rev() { println!("{}!", number); } println!("LIFTOFF!!!"); }` (the Book's countdown example at ch03-05-control-flow.md lines 538-544 verbatim modulo `"{number}!"` -> `"{}!", number` for consistency with lesson 011's positional shape) compiled with `rustc demo.rs` and run as `./demo` exits 0 silent and prints exactly four lines `3!`, `2!`, `1!`, `LIFTOFF!!!` — three lines from the loop body in descending order (the `1..4` range of lesson 022 reversed) then the `LIFTOFF!!!` line after the loop ends; the contrast probe with the same source modulo dropping the parens — `for number in 1..4.rev() { ... }` — fires `error[E0689]: can't call method `rev` on type `{integer}`` with `--> broken.rs:2:24` underlining `rev`, `help: you must surround the range in parentheses to call its `rev` function` and the source-diff showing `+ ` markers under the open paren before `1` and the close paren before `.rev()` — rustc parses `4.rev()` first because the method-call dot binds tighter than `..`; the auxiliary probe `(5..8).rev()` prints `7, 6, 5` (witnessing that reversal of an arbitrary `start..end` produces `end-1, ..., start`) and the auxiliary probe `(0..3).rev()` prints `n = 2, n = 1, n = 0, done` (witnessing the cleanest differential against lesson 022's `for i in 0..3` probe — same four-line pattern, three values reversed)
main_concept: appending `.rev()` (lesson 040's method-call form, empty arguments) to a parenthesized range value reverses the iteration order while preserving the same `for var in <range expression> { ... }` shape from lesson 022; concretely `(start..end).rev()` walks `end-1, end-2, ..., start` instead of `start, start+1, ..., end-1`; the parentheses are syntactically required because rustc's method-call dot binds tighter than the `..` range operator (without parens `1..4.rev()` parses as `1..(4.rev())` and rustc rejects with E0689 because `{integer}` has no `rev` method); the exclusive-upper-bound rule from lesson 022 carries through unchanged — reversing changes the order, not the membership, so `4` is still excluded from `(1..4).rev()`'s output; today is *name-and-use only* — `.rev()` is named as a method that reverses a range, with the trait machinery (`Iterator`, `DoubleEndedIterator`, the `Rev<Self>` return type) explicitly deferred per the Book's own framing "another method we've not yet talked about" at Ch3-5 line 533
depends_on: 022-for-range (load-bearing — `for var in 0..N { ... }` repeats the body once per number in the exclusive range with `var` auto-binding; today swaps the bare range for `(start..end).rev()` and observes reversed-order iteration with the same `for` shape; lesson 022's *What To Ignore For Now* explicitly named "Range methods like `.rev()`" as a deferred future move and today is that move), 040-method-call-syntax (load-bearing — the method-call form `value.method(args)` with receiver, dot, method name, parenthesized argument list; today applies that form to a range expression with empty arguments — receiver is `1..4`, method is `rev`, argument list is `()`; same shape as lesson 040's `n.abs()`), 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — `fn main` runs when the executable launches), 011-println-positional-args (cited — `println!("{}!", number)` reused for visible output), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (cited — diagnostic map applied to Probe 2's E0689 transcript), 001-rustc-compile-and-run (cited — `rustc demo.rs` then `./demo`, silent on success), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell)
unlocks: future "the `Iterator` trait as a centered concept — the trait machinery that supplies `.rev()`, `.map()`, `.filter()`, `.collect()`, etc. to ranges and collections; today's `.rev()` is one of dozens of methods on this trait" moves, future "`DoubleEndedIterator` as the specific trait that licenses `.rev()` — only iterators with a known end can be reversed" moves, future "other iterator methods on ranges — `.map()`, `.filter()`, `.collect()`, `.fold()`, `.take()`, `.skip()`, `.enumerate()`, `.sum()`, etc., each as its own move" moves, future "`(start..=end).rev()` — composition of today's `.rev()` with lesson 039's inclusive range, producing `end, end-1, ..., start`" moves, future "`(0..N).step_by(2)` and other range adapters — the `step_by` method named in lesson 022's *What To Ignore* alongside `.rev()`" moves, future "`.rev()` on collections — `Vec`, `String`, arrays (lesson 076), slices — same method works because they implement `IntoIterator` -> `Iterator` -> `DoubleEndedIterator`" moves, future "method chaining on iterators — `(0..10).rev().take(3)`, the iterator parallel to lesson 049's `String` chaining" moves, future "the precise precedence rule that makes `(1..4).rev()` require parens — the method-call dot binds tighter than `..` in Rust's grammar; mechanism-level, not learner-facing rule" moves, future "iterator adapters as a category vs iterator consumers — `.rev()`, `.map()`, `.filter()` return new iterators (lazy) while `.collect()`, `.sum()`, `.fold()` consume" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch03-05-control-flow.md
  - output/docs/rust/std/iter/trait.Iterator.md
  - output/docs/rust/std/ops/struct.Range.md
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/observations/091-range-reversal-rev.rs
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/evidence/091-range-reversal-rev.md
status: accepted
```

```text
id: 092-cargo-lock-reproducibility
move: read `Cargo.lock` as the file Cargo creates at the package root after the first `cargo build`/`cargo run`/`cargo check` to record the exact resolved version of every dependency the build picked; concretely the working probe `cargo new --vcs none lock_no_deps` then `cd lock_no_deps` then `cargo build` then `ls` then `cat Cargo.lock` produces a directory listing that includes `Cargo.lock` (absent in the pre-build `ls`, present in the post-build `ls` alongside `Cargo.toml`/`src/`/`target/`) and a 7-line lockfile starting `# This file is automatically @generated by Cargo. / # It is not intended for manual editing. / version = 4` followed by a single `[[package]] name = "lock_no_deps" version = "0.1.0"` block — the Book's "a bit sparse" no-dependency lockfile shape verbatim from Ch1-3 lines 139-143; the second `cargo build` immediately after produces the lesson-064 cache-hit shape (`Finished \`dev\` profile ... in 0.01s` only — no `Compiling`, no `Updating`, no rewrite of `Cargo.lock`) witnessing that Cargo silently reuses the existing lockfile; the corroborating Probe 2 with `rand = "0.8.5"` listed under `[dependencies]` (lesson 065) produces a 133-line `Cargo.lock` with one `[[package]]` per resolved transitive dependency (`rand v0.8.6`, `rand_chacha v0.3.1`, `rand_core v0.6.4`, `getrandom v0.2.17`, `libc v0.2.186`, `cfg-if v1.0.4`, `ppv-lite86 v0.2.21`, `zerocopy v0.8.48`, plus the `lock_with_rand` self-entry with `dependencies = [ "rand" ]`) — each entry carrying `source = "registry+https://github.com/rust-lang/crates.io-index"`, an exact `version` pin, and a sha256 `checksum` field; the contrast claim "without `Cargo.lock` the next build might pick newer matching versions" is grounded directly in Book Ch2 lines 587-606's bug-fix-with-regression counterfactual ("say that next week version 0.8.6 of the `rand` crate comes out, and that version contains an important bug fix, but it also contains a regression that will break your code") rather than a separate negative probe — the counterfactual cannot be witnessed locally without a time machine, and Probe 2's `Adding rand v0.8.6 (available: v0.10.1)` already shows the resolver examining multiple available versions
main_concept: `Cargo.lock` is Cargo's reproducible-build record; the first `cargo build` (or `cargo run`/`cargo check`) writes the exact resolved versions of every dependency the build picked into a TOML lockfile at the package root next to `Cargo.toml`; future builds see the lockfile and reuse those exact versions rather than re-resolving from `Cargo.toml`'s SemVer ranges, even if newer matching versions exist on crates.io — the Book's framing "your project will remain at 0.8.5 until you explicitly upgrade, thanks to the *Cargo.lock* file"; same source plus same lockfile gives the same compiled artifact regardless of when the build runs (reproducibility); even no-dependency packages get a sparse lockfile (one `[[package]]` for the package itself); the file is Cargo-managed, with its own header banner stating "This file is automatically @generated by Cargo. / It is not intended for manual editing." — do not hand-edit; for binary applications the Book recommends checking the lockfile into source control ("often checked into source control with the rest of the code in your project"); today is name-and-use-and-rule depth — the lockfile's TOML schema (`[[package]]` arrays, `source`, `checksum`, `dependencies` fields, `version = 4` schema marker), the `cargo update` command for explicit version bumps, the `--locked`/`--frozen` CI flags, the SemVer caret-range resolution algorithm, and the library-vs-binary checkin distinction are all explicitly deferred per the lesson's *What To Ignore For Now*
depends_on: 064-cargo-build-standalone (load-bearing — `cargo build` from inside a package directory; "the first `cargo build`" in today's claim is exactly lesson 064's invocation; the no-source-change cache-hit shape `Finished \`dev\` profile ... in 0.01s` only is reused as evidence of silent lockfile reuse), 065-cargo-toml-dependencies-entry (load-bearing — the `[dependencies]` section accepts `<crate-name> = "<version-string>"` entries like `rand = "0.8.5"`; the resolving-build transcript shape; lesson 065 explicitly named `Cargo.lock` and deferred it — today is that future move), 032-cargo-new-and-run (cited — `cargo new` scaffold and the `[package]` + empty `[dependencies]` shape of `Cargo.toml`), 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — the default `Hello, world!` program from `cargo new` is what Probe 1 builds), 011-println-positional-args (cited — same), ordinary computer-use (terminal, `cargo` on `PATH`, `cd`, `ls`, `cat` or text editor)
unlocks: future "`cargo update` — explicitly bump dependency versions, ignoring `Cargo.lock` and re-resolving from `Cargo.toml`'s SemVer ranges; the Book's next subsection at Ch2 lines 608ff" moves, future "SemVer caret-range resolution rules — `"0.8.5"` matches `0.8.5..0.9.0`; the algorithm Cargo uses to pick a version from `Cargo.toml`'s range; the deferral lesson 065 named explicitly" moves, future "`Cargo.lock`'s TOML schema as a centered concept — `[[package]]` arrays, `source`, `checksum`, `dependencies` fields, the `version = 4` schema marker; today's name-and-use becomes structural" moves, future "library-vs-binary lockfile-checkin convention — binary applications check `Cargo.lock` in; library crates published to crates.io often do not, so consumers can re-resolve" moves, future "`cargo build --locked` and `--frozen` for CI — fail the build if Cargo would have to change `Cargo.lock`; the operational form of today's reproducibility guarantee" moves, future "`cargo new --lib` and library packaging — the contrast that motivates the library-vs-binary checkin convention" moves, future "workspaces and workspace-level lockfiles — one `Cargo.lock` per workspace root; nested packages share it" moves, future "`[patch]` overrides and `[replace]` — sources of resolution that bypass crates.io but still go through the lockfile" moves, future "vendoring and `cargo build --offline` — operational uses of an existing lockfile without network access" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch01-03-hello-cargo.md
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch02-00-guessing-game-tutorial.md
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/observations/092-cargo-lock-reproducibility/
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/evidence/092-cargo-lock-reproducibility.md
status: accepted
```

```text
id: 093-standard-library-prelude
move: name the *standard library prelude* as the rule that decides which standard-library names work bare and which need a `use` declaration or a full path; concretely the working probe `fn main() { let s: String = String::new(); let v: Vec<i32> = Vec::new(); let r: Result<i32, String> = Ok(42); let opt: Option<i32> = Some(7); println!("s = {:?}", s); println!("v = {:?}", v); println!("r = {:?}", r); println!("opt = {:?}", opt); }` compiled with `rustc demo.rs` and run as `./demo` exits 0 silent and prints exactly four lines `s = ""`, `v = []`, `r = Ok(42)`, `opt = Some(7)` — every name on the right of an `=` (`String`, `Vec`, `Ok`, `Some`) is reached with no `use` line and no `std::` prefix because all four names are members of the standard library prelude that rustc implicitly imports into every module; the contrast probe `fn main() { let m = HashMap::new(); }` fires `error[E0433]: cannot find type `HashMap` in this scope` with `--> broken.rs:2:13` underlining `HashMap`, `help: consider importing this struct`, and the source-diff `1 + use std::collections::HashMap;` — the same `Type::new()` shape that Probe 1 compiled silently here fails because `HashMap` is not in the prelude; the `help:` line literally suggests the lesson-044 `use` mechanism that would put it in scope, witnessing that names outside the prelude need either `use` or a full path (lesson 050)
main_concept: a *prelude* is "a collection of names that are automatically brought into scope of every module in a crate" (Reference, names/preludes line 8); the *standard library prelude* is the prelude that consists of the names from a single standard library module — `std::prelude::rust_2024` for the default `cargo new` 2024-edition crate per the Reference's edition table — and rustc implicitly imports it into every module of every crate; the rule that splits standard-library names is binary: a name is either in the prelude (write it bare, no `use` line, no `std::` prefix — `String`, `Vec`, `Option`/`Some`/`None`, `Result`/`Ok`/`Err` are the load-bearing members; the lesson does not enumerate the rest) or it is not (use a full path like `std::io::stdin()` per lesson 050, or a `use` declaration like `use std::io;` per lesson 044); the existence of the rule is *why* lesson 042's `String::new()` worked bare and lesson 052's `Ok(n)`/`Err(n)` worked bare while lesson 050's `std::io::stdin()` needed the full path; today is name-the-rule depth — the prelude's full enumeration, edition-specific differences (the 2021/2024 preludes added `TryInto`/`TryFrom`/`FromIterator` traits over earlier editions), the four other preludes named in the Reference (extern, language, `macro_use`, tool), `#![no_std]`, `#![no_implicit_prelude]`, glob imports, prelude re-exports, and the `Display` vs `Debug` trait distinction (which `{:?}` brushes against) are all explicitly deferred per the lesson's *What To Ignore For Now*
depends_on: 042-string-new (load-bearing — `String::new()` worked as a bare `Type::name()` call with no `use` line; today says the prelude is *why* that works, with `String` as a load-bearing prelude member; lesson 042's *What To Ignore* named "*The standard prelude*" as a deferred item — today is that move), 044-use-declaration (load-bearing — the file-top-level `use Path::final;` form that brings the final segment of a path into scope; today's role: the mechanism for any standard-library name *not* in the prelude; lesson 044's *What To Ignore* also named "*The standard prelude*" — today is that move), 050-io-stdin-handle (load-bearing — the full-path call form `std::io::stdin()` reached a free function with no `use` line; today says the prelude is *why* that requires the full path: `std::io::stdin` is not in the prelude; lesson 050's *What To Ignore* named "*The standard prelude*" — today is that move), 052-result-enum-and-is-ok (load-bearing — `Result<T, E>` with `Ok`/`Err` constructors worked bare; lesson 052's body and *Mental Model Delta* both noted in passing that "`Result` (along with `Ok` and `Err`) is in the *prelude*"; today centers that framing as its own concept rather than a parenthetical), 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — `fn main` is the entry point), 005-let-binding (cited — `let name: TYPE = value;`), 011-println-positional-args (cited — `println!` with a `{}` slot; today extends by one new formatter `{:?}`, glossed in one sentence as the Debug formatter), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (cited — diagnostic map applied to the E0433 contrast transcript), 001-rustc-compile-and-run (cited — `rustc demo.rs` then `./demo`, silent on success), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell)
unlocks: future "the `Display` vs `Debug` trait distinction as a centered concept — `{}` requires `Display`, `{:?}` requires `Debug`; today brushed against the distinction by using `{:?}` on `String`/`Vec`/`Result`/`Option` but did not unpack the trait machinery" moves, future "the full enumeration of `std::prelude::rust_2024` — `Box`, `Drop`, `Default`, `Iterator`, `IntoIterator`, `From`, `Into`, `TryFrom`, `TryInto`, `FromIterator`, `Eq`, `Ord`, `Hash`, `Copy`, `Clone`, etc.; today named only `String`, `Vec`, `Option`/`Some`/`None`, `Result`/`Ok`/`Err`" moves, future "the *language prelude* — `bool`/`char`/`str`/`i32`/`i64`/`u32`/`usize`/`isize`/`f32`/`f64` etc. as built-in type names always in scope (Reference names/preludes lines 142-164); today only the standard library prelude was named" moves, future "the *extern prelude* — external crates added by `--extern` or by Cargo's `[dependencies]`; the `core` and `std` crates being implicitly in the extern prelude" moves, future "the *`macro_use` prelude* and the *tool prelude* — Reference's two remaining preludes named in lines 16-20" moves, future "`#![no_std]` — the crate-level attribute that swaps `std::prelude::*` for `core::prelude::*` and excludes the `std` crate from the extern prelude; useful for bare-metal or embedded targets" moves, future "`#![no_implicit_prelude]` — the module-level attribute that turns off implicit prelude import for a crate or module" moves, future "edition-specific prelude differences — the 2021/2024 preludes added `TryInto`/`TryFrom`/`FromIterator` over earlier editions; the edition keyword in `Cargo.toml` selects which prelude module is in scope" moves, future "glob imports `use std::collections::*;` and how they interact with the prelude — the Reference's panic-hack note about user-written glob imports taking precedence over prelude names to resolve ambiguity" moves, future "re-exporting the prelude from a custom module — `pub use std::prelude::v1::*;` for a library that wants to ship its own prelude module" moves, future "`std::collections::HashMap` as the canonical contrast-probe target — full move on the type, its `new()` constructor, and the difference from `Vec`'s prelude membership" moves, future "the `Box<T>` heap-allocation type — named in the Reference's prelude discussion (line 10) but not yet in the audience's vocabulary; alongside `Drop`, the trait-level half of `Box`'s story" moves, future "the `Default` trait and `String::default()` — another route to an empty `String`, lesson 042 deferred it; `Default` is in the prelude" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/reference/names/preludes.md
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/lessons/052-result-enum-and-is-ok.md
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/observations/093-standard-library-prelude.rs
```

```text
id: 094-unused-must-use-result
move: recognize the `unused_must_use` warning that fires when a function returning `Result<T, E>` is called as an expression statement and the value is discarded — and name `let _ = expr;` as the documented escape hatch; concretely the working probe `use std::io; fn main() { let mut buf = String::new(); io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf); println!("got: {}", buf); }` (lesson 054's program with the `.expect("Failed to read line")` call removed) compiled with `rustc demo.rs` produces the bordered diagnostic `warning: unused \`Result\` that must be used` with `--> demo.rs:5:5` underlining `io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf);`, `= note: this \`Result\` may be an \`Err\` variant, which should be handled`, `= note: \`#[warn(unused_must_use)]\` (part of \`#[warn(unused)]\`) on by default`, and `help: use \`let _ = ...\` to ignore the resulting value` showing the source diff `5 |     let _ = io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf);` / `  |     +++++++` — `rustc` exits 0, the trailer is `warning: 1 warning emitted` (not `error: aborting due to N previous error(s)`), the `demo` executable is produced, and `echo "hello" | ./demo` prints `got: hello` and exits 0 (lesson 069's category); the contrast probe replaces line 5 with `let _ = io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf);` and `rustc demo_silenced.rs` compiles silently with no warning, witnessing that `let _ = expr;` is the deliberate-discard form the `help:` line literally suggests; the negative contrast probe `fn maybe() -> Option<i32> { Some(7) } fn main() { maybe(); }` compiles silently with no `unused_must_use` warning, witnessing that the lint is bound to `#[must_use]` types (which `Result<T, E>` is and `Option<T>` is not), not to all enums-with-payloads
main_concept: the `unused_must_use` lint detects "unused result of a type flagged as `#[must_use]`" (rustc lint listing line 5744) and is in the warn-by-default group, so a discarded `Result<T, E>` value at expression-statement position fires a `warning:`-headlined diagnostic at compile time but does not abort the build (lesson 069's category); the lint exists because a discarded `Result` is usually a bug — the call could have been an `Err` variant whose failure information is being thrown away (Book ch02 line 383 "Rust warns that you haven't used the `Result` value returned from `read_line`, indicating that the program hasn't handled a possible error"); the `help:` line in the diagnostic suggests `let _ = ...` and that form is the documented escape hatch — `let _ = expr;` is an expression statement whose left-hand side names the placeholder `_`, which `rustc` accepts as "the value is bound (and immediately dropped)" and so the lint sees the value as used; today installs only the *exact shape* `let _ = expr;` for the `unused_must_use` discard case, and explicitly does not install `_` as a centered pattern token (its broader role on the LEFT of `let`, in `match` arm wildcards, and in tuple destructures is a future move) and does not install authoring `#[must_use]` on user-defined types (Reference attributes/diagnostics lines 404-447) — those are deferred; this lesson is one specific lint in the warn-by-default group, joining `unused_variables` (lesson 069) and `non_snake_case` (lesson 089) as the third specific lint named in this run, without reopening the broader lint-system deferrals (`#[allow(...)]`/`#[deny(...)]`, the `-A`/`-D`/`-W`/`-F` flags, the level taxonomy, lint groups in general, the `?` operator, alternative consumers `match`/`if let`, the `io::Result<T>` type alias, `Option<T>` and other non-`#[must_use]` types, other `#[must_use]` types in std like `MutexGuard`, the `#[must_use = "msg"]` message form)
depends_on: 069-rustc-warnings (load-bearing — `warning:` is a separate category from `error:`; warnings do not abort the build, `rustc` exits 0, an executable is produced; today's diagnostic is exactly that category and the trailer `warning: 1 warning emitted` (not `error: aborting due to N previous error(s)`) is lesson 069's signal; today is the third specific warn-by-default lint named in this run after lesson 069's `unused_variables` and lesson 089's `non_snake_case`), 052-result-enum-and-is-ok (load-bearing — `Result<T, E>` as a two-variant enum `Ok(T)`, `Err(E)`; the lint's name "unused `Result`" attaches because today's discarded value is a `Result`; lesson 052's vocabulary — variant, constructor, type parameter, prelude — carries through unchanged; no new claim about `Result` is introduced today), 053-result-expect-and-panic (load-bearing — `.expect("msg")` consumes a `Result` by panicking on `Err`; today's program is lesson 053's chain *without* `.expect(...)` and that omission is what triggers the lint; lesson 053 framed `.expect` as the way to *get the payload out* and today fills in what `rustc` does when no consumer is chained at all), 054-read-line-from-stdin (load-bearing — `io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf)` returns a `Result<usize, io::Error>`; today's probe is lesson 054's full chain `io::stdin().read_line(&mut buf).expect("Failed to read line");` with the `.expect(...)` call removed, making the `Result` discardable), 050-io-stdin-handle (cited — `std::io::stdin()` shape; `use std::io;`), 044-use-declaration (cited — `use Path::final;` form; the probe uses `use std::io;`), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (cited — the four-part diagnostic map applied here to a `warning:`-headlined block: headline / `-->` location / source excerpt with caret / `help:` and `= note:` lines), 011-println-positional-args (cited — `println!` with a `{}` slot; the probe uses `println!("got: {}", buf);`), 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — `fn main` is the entry point), 005-let-binding (cited — `let name = value;`; today extends to `let _ = expr;` as the placeholder-name form for deliberate discard, naming the exact shape but not the broader `_` semantics), 070-rustc-explain (cited only — *What To Ignore For Now* names `rustc --explain unused_must_use` as a non-applicable form, since `--explain` is for `E####` codes only and lints have no `E####`), 089-ch3-3-function-conventions (cited only as the run's prior named warn-by-default lint, `non_snake_case`), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell; plus shell-piping `echo "hello" | ./demo` — assumption used since lesson 054)
unlocks: future "the `_` token as a centered concept — its role as the discard placeholder on the LEFT of `let` (`let _ = expr;`), as the wildcard pattern in `match` arms, and in tuple destructures (lesson 073 brushed against the pattern-position role); today named only the exact `let _ = expr;` shape" moves, future "authoring `#[must_use]` on user-defined types, functions, and traits (Reference attributes/diagnostics lines 404-507) — the `#[must_use]` attribute itself, the `#[must_use = \"msg\"]` message form, and the type/function/trait position rules" moves, future "the `?` operator — the *other* short way to handle a `Result` besides `.expect` (lesson 053) and `match`; propagates the `Err` to the caller without panicking, and silences `unused_must_use` because the value is consumed" moves, future "alternative consumers of a `Result` that also silence `unused_must_use` — `match expr { Ok(v) => ..., Err(e) => ... }` and `if let Ok(_) = expr { ... }`; both compose already-installed lessons (058 will install full match-on-payload-variants, and `if let` is its own future move)" moves, future "the lint level system as a centered concept — `#[allow(unused_must_use)]`, `#[deny(unused_must_use)]`, `#[forbid(...)]`, the `-A`/`-D`/`-W`/`-F` flags, and the `Reference` lint-levels page; deferred since lesson 069, and today's lint is the third reachable trigger for that move" moves, future "the lint-group taxonomy — the parenthetical `(part of \`#[warn(unused)]\`)` in today's `= note:` line names the `unused` lint group; the broader group structure (`unused`, `nonstandard_style`, `future_incompatible`, etc.) and how groups compose is its own move" moves, future "the `io::Result<T>` type alias and `io::Error` type — lesson 054 already deferred these; today's `Result<usize, io::Error>` framing inherits unchanged" moves, future "other `#[must_use]` types in std beyond `Result` — `MutexGuard`, `RwLockReadGuard`, `BorrowMut`, `MaybeUninit`, etc.; today named only `Result` and explicitly excluded `Option<T>` from `#[must_use]`" moves, future "`cargo fix` and `cargo clippy --fix` — automated application of `help:`-suggested fixes including `let _ = ...` for `unused_must_use`; deferred since lesson 069 and lesson 087's rustfmt neighborhood" moves, future "panic-vs-warning escalation — `#![deny(unused_must_use)]` at the crate level promotes today's warning into a hard error that does abort the build; same lint, different level (lesson 069 deferred); the move-into-error pattern is shared with all warn-by-default lints" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/rustc/lints/listing/warn-by-default.md
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch02-00-guessing-game-tutorial.md
  - output/docs/rust/reference/attributes/diagnostics.md
  - experimental/eduratchet2/runs/rust-moves/lessons/069-rustc-warnings.md
```

```text
id: 095-struct-with-named-fields
move: declare a new type with `struct Name { field: Type, ... }` at module scope, build one instance with the struct expression `Name { field: value, ... }`, and read a field with `instance.field`; concretely the working probe `struct Point { x: i32, y: i32, } fn main() { let p = Point { x: 3, y: 7 }; println!("p.x = {}, p.y = {}", p.x, p.y); }` compiled with `rustc demo.rs` and run as `./demo` exits 0 silent and prints `p.x = 3, p.y = 7` — the three composed pieces (declaration, construction, field access) all witnessed in one minimal program; the contrast probe with the same struct declaration but `let p = Point { x: 3 };` (`y` dropped from the construction expression) fires `error[E0063]: missing field \`y\` in initializer of \`Point\`` with `--> missing.rs:7:13` underlining `Point` (the struct name token), trailer `error: aborting due to 1 previous error`, witnessing the rule "every field declared in the struct must be given a value at construction"; the auxiliary order-doesn't-matter probe `let p = Point { y: 7, x: 3 };` compiles and prints byte-identically to the working probe (Book ch05-01 line 34 "We don't have to specify the fields in the same order in which we declared them in the struct"); the secondary contrast probe `let p = Point { x: 3, y: 7 }; println!("p.z = {}", p.z);` fires `error[E0609]: no field \`z\` on type \`Point\`` with `help: a field with a similar name exists` and the source-diff `+ p.x`, witnessing the field-names-belong-to-the-type rule the lesson's *Mental Model Delta* installs (lesson does not center this contrast — kept as evidence-only for verification)
main_concept: a *struct with named fields* is the smallest user-defined product type in Rust; one centered claim with three coupled pieces under Book ch05-01 lines 4-66 (load-bearing) and Reference items/structs.md lines 14-44 (load-bearing). (1) *Declaration*: `struct Name { field: Type, ... }` at module scope (a *struct item*, like `fn` is a *function item*) introduces a new nominal type called `Name` whose values carry one piece of data per named field; the field list lives in curly braces with `IDENTIFIER : Type` pairs separated by commas, with optional trailing comma per the Reference grammar. (2) *Construction*: `Name { field: value, ... }` is a *struct expression* (Reference expressions/struct-expr.md) that produces one instance of the type by giving each declared field a value; every declared field must appear exactly once at construction (witnessed by Probe 2's E0063 contrast); the order of `key: value` pairs is free (witnessed by Probe 3); the resulting value sits on the right of `=` like any other expression and binds with `let p = ...;` (lesson 005's binding form, unmodified). (3) *Field access*: `instance.field` is a *field expression* (Reference expressions/field-expr.md) that evaluates to the value stored in that field; the whole expression has the field's declared type, so it slots into any expression position (`let`, `println!` argument list, right of `=`); field expressions cannot be followed by a parenthesized comma-separated list — that would parse as a method call (Reference `expr.field.not-method-call`). Today's load-bearing adjacent-but-distinct claim: field access has no parentheses (`p.x`); method calls always have parentheses (`p.x()`). The two share the dot but are syntactically distinct. The audience crosses from "type names refer to library-built things" (lessons 042 String, 093 Vec) to "I declare a type." Today is *shallow operational*: install only the three composed pieces with primitive field types (`i32`); explicitly defer `pub`/visibility, tuple structs, unit-like structs, struct update syntax, `#[derive(...)]`, `impl` blocks/methods, struct pattern destructuring, field mutation, field-init shorthand, generics on structs, lifetime-annotated reference fields, owned/borrowed types as field types (`String`/`&str`/`Vec<T>`), enums, and move/drop semantics for struct values. This unlocks reading struct declarations in the rmp target repo (`struct Bones { upper: u64, lower: u64 }`, `struct ParseBigUIntError {}`, etc.) per the rmp-target-audit recommendation §11 first-move; trait machinery, `pub`, generics, lifetimes, and `Vec<T>` field types remain blocked downstream.
depends_on: 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — `fn main` is the entry point; the probe uses one `fn main` block, unchanged), 005-let-binding (load-bearing — `let p = expression;` binds `p` to the value of `expression`; today's `let p = Point { x: 3, y: 7 };` is the same form with a struct-expression right-hand side; nothing about the binding form changes), 011-println-positional-args (load-bearing — each `{}` is a positional placeholder consumed by the next extra argument; lesson 011 explicitly said any expression can sit in the argument list and used `a + b` directly; today plugs `p.x` and `p.y` into the slots — both are expressions of type `i32`), 019-type-annotation-i32 (load-bearing — `i32` is the 32-bit signed integer type; the `field: Type` slot in the struct declaration is the same `: TYPE` machinery from lesson 019, repurposed: lesson 019 applied it to a `let` binding, today applies it to a struct field declaration), 040-method-call-syntax (load-bearing — the dot operator binds a *receiver* expression to a method name with a parenthesized argument list; today's *no parens after the dot for field access* rule explicitly contrasts against lesson 040: `p.x` reads a field; `p.x()` would call a method named `x`; the two surfaces share the dot but differ on the trailing parenthesized argument list), 001-rustc-compile-and-run (cited — `rustc demo.rs` then `./demo`, silent on success), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (cited — diagnostic four-part map applied to Probe 2's E0063 transcript and Probe 4's E0609 transcript), 042-string-new (cited only — *The Move*'s motivating sentence "Lesson 042 used `String`, an instance of a type the standard library already declared"; no claim about `String` is reused), 069-rustc-warnings (cited only — Probe 2's `error: aborting due to 1 previous error` trailer is read with lesson 069's category map, distinguishing from `warning:` category), 093-standard-library-prelude (cited only — *The Move*'s motivating sentence "Lesson 093 named `Vec<i32>` the same way" as a parallel; no claim about prelude membership is reused), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell)
unlocks: future "the `pub` keyword on items, struct fields, and modules — `pub struct Foo { pub x: i32 }` and the visibility-modifier grammar position the Reference structs.md line 22 names; the smallest atomic move in the audit's §11 chain after struct definition" moves, future "visibility paths `pub(super)` / `pub(crate)` — restricted-visibility forms used heavily in the rmp target" moves, future "tuple structs `struct Foo(T1, T2);` — fields by position, accessed with `.0`/`.1`; Book ch05-01 lines 277-313" moves, future "unit-like structs `struct Foo;` — no fields at all; Book ch05-01 lines 316-344" moves, future "struct update syntax `Foo { x: 1, ..other }` — copy remaining fields from another instance; Book ch05-01 lines 181-273; explicit move-vs-copy semantics deferred until ownership vocabulary lands" moves, future "the `#[derive(...)]` attribute (`Debug`, `Clone`, `Copy`, `PartialEq`) — downstream of the trait machinery in Q07's deferred queue" moves, future "`impl Type { fn method(&self, ...) -> Type { ... } }` inherent-method authoring — uses today's struct as the type and lesson 040's method-call form as the consumer; audit §11 chain item 5" moves, future "receiver forms `self`, `&self`, `&mut self` — the parameter-list shapes that distinguish consume/borrow/mutate; audit §11 chain item 6" moves, future "struct pattern destructuring `let Point { x, y } = p;` and `match p { Point { x, y } => ... }` — uses lesson 058's match-on-payload-variants and lesson 073's tuple-destructure as parallel forms" moves, future "the `..` rest token in struct patterns" moves, future "field-init shorthand `Foo { x, y }` when local names match field names — Book Listing 5-5; cosmetic shortcut" moves, future "field mutation `let mut p = ...; p.x = 5;` — composes lesson 006's `mut` and today's field access in lvalue position; Book Listing 5-3" moves, future "generic structs `struct Foo<T> { x: T }` — type parameters on structs; downstream of generic-types install" moves, future "lifetime-annotated reference fields `struct Foo<'a> { name: &'a str }` — Book ch05-01 lines 346-418 explicitly defers this to Chapter 10; downstream of references-deeper install" moves, future "structs holding `String`, `&str`, or `Vec<T>` — owned and borrowed string/collection field types; raises ownership and lifetime questions deferred until those arcs open" moves, future "enum definition `enum Sign { Positive, Negative }` and `enum BigInt { Zero, Nonzero(Nonzero) }` — the parallel data-type vocabulary; audit §11 chain item 4; the next natural move after this one" moves, future "move/drop semantics for struct values when passed to or returned from a function — composes lesson 020's parameter machinery with ownership rules; required for reading rmp's `fn build(...) -> BigInt { ... }` style" moves, future "the rmp target's first readable struct lines — `struct BigUInt { limbs: Vec<u64> }`, `struct Bones { upper: u64, lower: u64 }`, `struct Nonzero { sign: Sign, mantissa: BigUInt }`, `struct ParseBigUIntError {}` — composes today's struct definition with deferred `pub`/`Vec<u64>`/`Sign`/`BigUInt`" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch05-01-defining-structs.md
  - output/docs/rust/reference/items/structs.md
```

```text
id: 096-inline-module-and-pub
move: declare an inline submodule with `mod foo { ... }` at the crate root, mark one item inside it with `pub` (`pub fn hi() { ... }`), and reach the item from `fn main` outside the module via the path `foo::hi()`; concretely the working probe `mod foo { pub fn hi() { println!("hi from foo"); } } fn main() { foo::hi(); }` compiled with `rustc demo.rs` and run as `./demo` exits 0 silent and prints `hi from foo` — both coupled pieces (inline submodule + public-marked inner function) witnessed in one minimal program; the contrast probe with the same source modulo `pub fn hi()` -> `fn hi()` (one keyword removed at the same definition site, call site unchanged) fires `error[E0603]: function \`hi\` is private` with `--> broken.rs:8:10` underlining `hi` at the *use site* (column 10 of the `foo::hi();` call), trailer `error: aborting due to 1 previous error`, plus a `note: the function \`hi\` is defined here` block with a second `-->` line `broken.rs:2:5` underlining `fn hi()` at the definition site, witnessing the rule "without `pub`, the function exists, the path resolves to it, but crossing the module boundary is rejected at compile time"; the auxiliary E0425 probe with the same `pub fn hi()` definition but the call site dropped to bare `hi();` (no `foo::` prefix) fires `error[E0425]: cannot find function \`hi\` in this scope` with `help: consider importing this function` and source-diff `+ use foo::hi;`, witnessing the framing "items inside the module live in a *new namespace called* `foo`" without re-installing lesson 044's `use`; the calibration probe with `fn hi()` at the crate root and no `mod foo { ... }` block compiles silently and prints `hi`, identical to `pub fn hi()` at the crate root — empirical justification that a single-binary `rustc` build needs a module boundary for `pub`'s rule to be observable
main_concept: items inside a module are *private to the module by default*; `pub` before an item declaration is what makes it accessible from outside via `module::item`; one centered claim with two coupled pieces under Book Ch7-2 lines 41-44 (load-bearing, the private-vs-public rule) and Book Ch7-2 lines 127-152 (load-bearing, the inline `mod NAME { ... }` syntax) and Book Ch7-3 lines 121-127 (load-bearing, the privacy-check failure mode) and Book Ch7-3 lines 142-156 (load-bearing, `pub` exposing items) and Book Ch7-3 lines 215-217 (load-bearing, "privacy rules apply to ... functions ... as well as modules") and Reference items/modules.md lines 10-15 (load-bearing, the formal `mod` grammar — both inline and file-based forms) and lines 19-23 (load-bearing, "a module is a container for zero or more items") and Reference visibility-and-privacy.md lines 9-15 (load-bearing, the formal `Visibility` grammar) and lines 29-31 (load-bearing, "By default, everything is *private*") and lines 52-56 (load-bearing, the access rules) and error_codes/E0603.md (load-bearing, the corpus's verbatim `mod foo { ... }`/`foo::PRIVATE` shape with `pub` as the documented fix). (1) *Inline submodule declaration*: `mod foo { ... }` at module scope (a *module item*, like `fn` is a *function item*) introduces a new named submodule whose body lives in a brace-enclosed block; items inside the body (functions, structs, more modules, etc.) live in a new namespace called by the module name. The Reference's `Module` grammar admits two shapes — semicolon-terminated `mod foo;` (file-based; deferred to lesson 097) and brace-enclosed `mod foo { ... }` (inline; today's form). (2) *`pub` on a function item*: items inside a module are private by default per the Reference's privacy rule "By default, everything is *private*"; declaring an item with `pub` makes it accessible from outside the module per Book Ch7-3 line 140. The audience already knows the call form `module::name(args)` from lesson 043; today's contribution is the rule that makes the call site succeed or fail. The Book itself walks through this in three listings (7-3 → 7-5/7-6 → 7-7) showing that path resolution is not the same as access permission; today's lesson collapses this into one move because the outer module sits at the crate root in a single-binary build and only the *inner* item's visibility is load-bearing for the contrast. The audience crosses from "modules are namespaces the standard library hands me" (lessons 043, 044) to "I author my own module; items inside it are private by default; `pub` lets one item out." Today is *shallow operational*: install only the bare `pub` form on a function item inside an inline `mod foo { ... }` block, with the E0603 contrast as the centered teaching point. Explicitly defer file-based modules `mod foo;` (lesson 097), restricted visibility `pub(super)` / `pub(crate)` / `pub(in path)` / `pub(self)`, visibility on the `mod` declaration itself `pub mod foo { ... }`, `pub` on struct fields, `pub` on enum variants, `pub use` re-exports, `pub trait` and `pub impl`, the `crate::` / `super::` / `self::` path prefixes, nested submodules, privacy-by-default at the crate root (real but unobservable in a single-binary build, the lesson's calibration probe captures this), the `Visibility?` grammar slot on every other item kind (struct, enum, union, const, static, mod, use, trait, etc.). This unlocks reading the rmp target's `pub mod bigint;` / `pub mod biguint;` / `pub use basic::BigUInt;` / `pub fn zero()` / `pub fn is_zero(&self) -> bool` lines per the rmp-target-audit recommendation; `pub mod`, `pub use`, `pub(super)`, file-based modules, and `pub` on struct fields remain blocked downstream and are listed as deferred future moves.
depends_on: 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — `fn main` is the entry point; the probe uses one `fn main` block, unchanged), 008-define-and-call-function (cited — the definition shape `fn name() { ... }` is unchanged today; the auxiliary E0425 probe witnesses what happens when the call site is bare `hi();` with the function defined inside a module), 011-println-positional-args (cited — `println!` with one `{}` slot consumed by no extra argument; the body of `hi` is the simplest possible body), 043-nested-module-paths (load-bearing — the call form `module::name(args)`; today's `foo::hi` is that shape with the user's own module on the left of `::`; lesson 043's *What To Ignore For Now* explicitly named "Defining your own modules — `mod`, inline `{ ... }` modules, and modules in separate files" and "Visibility and `pub`" as deferred future moves; today is the first half of those — inline `mod` plus bare `pub` — leaving file-based modules and restricted visibility deferred), 044-use-declaration (cited only — lesson 044 is named in the *Prerequisites* section as a close cousin already seen; the contrast probe's `help:` block proposes `use foo::hi;` as one conceivable fix, but the lesson body explicitly says this is lesson 044's mechanism applied to the user's own module rather than a new move; no `use` line appears in any committed probe), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (load-bearing — the four-part diagnostic map applied to Probe 2's E0603 transcript; today's diagnostic is the first one in the run with a `note:` block carrying a second `-->` line that points at a *definition* site rather than a use site, which lesson 003 admits as "diagnostics may show more than one `-->` line"), 001-rustc-compile-and-run (cited — `rustc demo.rs` then `./demo`, silent on success), 069-rustc-warnings (cited only — Probe 2's `error: aborting due to 1 previous error` trailer is read with lesson 069's category map, distinguishing from `warning:` category), 095-struct-with-named-fields (cited only — the lesson's *What To Ignore For Now* bullet "today only puts `pub` on the function, not on a field" composes today's move with lesson 095's struct declaration and is deferred), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell)
unlocks: future "file-based modules — `mod foo;` (semicolon-terminated, no body) resolves to `foo.rs` or `foo/mod.rs` next to the source file; the natural follow-on (lesson 097) for today's inline form, with the same `mod` keyword and same privacy rule but body in a separate file" moves, future "`pub mod foo;` and `pub mod foo { ... }` — making the module declaration itself public; the rmp target's `lib.rs` uses this with `pub mod bigint; pub mod biguint;` to expose its top-level modules to the binary crate via `bignum::bigint::BigInt`" moves, future "restricted visibility `pub(super)` — make an item visible only to the parent module; the rmp target uses this heavily for struct fields like `pub(super) limbs: Vec<u64>`" moves, future "restricted visibility `pub(crate)` — make an item visible everywhere within the current crate but not outside it; common in library crates with internal helpers" moves, future "restricted visibility `pub(in path)` and `pub(self)` — the remaining two shapes from the Reference's `Visibility` grammar" moves, future "`pub` on struct fields — `struct Foo { pub x: i32 }`; composes today's `pub` keyword with lesson 095's struct declaration; the visibility position is per-field" moves, future "`pub` on enum variants — variants of a `pub` enum are public by default per Reference visibility-and-privacy.md line 31, but plain `pub enum` itself is its own move and depends on enums being installed" moves, future "`pub use Path::Item;` re-exports — composes today's `pub` with lesson 044's `use`; allows a module to re-export an item under a shorter path; the rmp target's `biguint/mod.rs` uses `pub use basic::BigUInt;`" moves, future "`pub trait` and `pub impl` blocks — trait visibility, blocked until the trait arc opens" moves, future "`crate::` as a path root — the absolute-path form starting from the current crate root, alternative to the relative path used today" moves, future "`super::` path prefix — relative path starting from the parent module, useful for sibling-module navigation inside a module body; the rmp target uses `super::` extensively in its multi-file `biguint/` module" moves, future "`self::` path prefix — relative path starting from the current module, occasionally useful to disambiguate" moves, future "nested submodules `mod foo { mod bar { ... } }` — composition of today's rule with itself; the Book's `front_of_house { hosting { ... } serving { ... } }` example in Listing 7-1" moves, future "the privacy chain rule for nested modules — Reference visibility-and-privacy.md lines 52-56's 'access all the item's ancestor modules' rule unpacks why a deep `pub` item still requires every ancestor on the path to be reachable" moves, future "binary + library crate packaging — `lib.rs` exporting modules consumed by `main.rs` via `bignum::bigint::BigInt`; the rmp target's organizational pattern" moves, future "the `#[allow(unused)]` attribute on a private module — silencing the dead-code lint when a module is intentionally not yet wired up" moves, future "the rmp target's first readable `pub` lines — `pub mod bigint;` and `pub mod biguint;` in `lib.rs`, `pub use basic::BigUInt;` in `biguint/mod.rs`, `pub fn zero() -> Self` and `pub fn is_zero(&self) -> bool` in `biguint/basic.rs` — composes today's `pub` with deferred `pub mod`, `pub use`, and method-receiver-on-`Self` machinery" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch07-02-defining-modules-to-control-scope-and-privacy.md
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch07-03-paths-for-referring-to-an-item-in-the-module-tree.md
  - output/docs/rust/reference/items/modules.md
```

```text
id: 097-file-based-module
move: declare a submodule using the file-based form `mod foo;` (semicolon, no braces) at the top of `main.rs` and place its body in a sibling file `foo.rs` next to `main.rs`; concretely with `main.rs` containing `mod foo; fn main() { foo::hi(); }` and `foo.rs` containing `pub fn hi() { println!("hi from foo"); }`, the command `rustc main.rs` run from the directory holding both files compiles silently and `./main` prints `hi from foo` (byte-identical to lesson 096's inline-form output) and exits 0; the contrast probe with `foo.rs` renamed away (so the file `rustc` is told to look for is missing) fires `error[E0583]: file not found for module \`foo\`` with `--> main.rs:1:1` underlining the whole `mod foo;` declaration, a `help:` block reading `to create the module \`foo\`, create file "foo.rs" or "foo/mod.rs"`, a `note:` block on the alternative `mod foo` elsewhere in the crate case, plus the standard `error: aborting due to 1 previous error` and `--explain E0583` trailer; the auxiliary carry-through probe with `foo.rs` present but `pub` deleted from `fn hi` fires the lesson-096 `error[E0603]: function \`hi\` is private` diagnostic now spanning two files (use site `--> main.rs:4:10` underlining `hi`, definition site `--> foo.rs:1:1` underlining `fn hi()` in the `note:` block) — concrete evidence that the privacy rule from lesson 096 carries through unchanged across the file boundary
main_concept: the file-based form of the `Module` grammar rule. The Reference's `Module` grammar at items/modules.md lines 9-15 admits two shapes — `mod NAME;` (semicolon-terminated, body loaded from a separate file) and `mod NAME { ... }` (brace-enclosed, inline). Lesson 096 installed the brace form. Today installs the semicolon form. The single new piece is the source-layout convention: `mod foo;` (with semicolon, no body) tells `rustc` to load the module body from `foo.rs` adjacent to the declaring source file, per Reference items/modules.md lines 70-81 ("A module without a body is loaded from an external file. ... the module's contents are in a file with the name of the module plus the `.rs` extension") and Book ch07-05 lines 14-30, 34-37 ("Remove the code inside the curly brackets ... leaving only the `mod NAME;` declaration ... place the code that was in the curly brackets into a new file named *NAME.rs*. The compiler knows to look in this file because it came across the module declaration ... with the name `NAME`"). Everything else from lesson 096 carries through unchanged: the privacy-by-default rule, `pub`'s effect, and the `module::item` access form (Probe 3 in the evidence appendix witnesses E0603 across the file boundary, identical to lesson 096's E0603 modulo the `note:` line's `-->` pointing at the sibling file rather than back into the same source). The Book at lines 49-56 names a load-bearing negative claim — "`mod` is *not* an `include` operation" — meaning files in the same directory that no `mod` line ever names are simply not part of the build; only the `mod foo;` declaration makes `rustc` aware of `foo.rs`. New E-code in the run's collection: E0583 ("file not found for module"), captured verbatim in Probe 2, with `help:` block naming both candidate filenames `foo.rs` (today) and `foo/mod.rs` (deferred subdirectory form). Today is *shallow operational*: install only the file-name rule for the top-level `foo.rs` adjacency case, with the E0583 contrast as the centered teaching point. Explicitly defer the subdirectory `foo/mod.rs` form (Reference items/modules.md lines 82-88, used by the rmp target's `biguint/`), nested file-based modules (a file-based module body containing its own `mod bar;`), `pub mod foo;` making the module declaration itself public (already deferred in 096), the `#[path = "..."]` attribute, edition-specific path-resolution differences (Rust 2018 vs 2015; this run uses 2024), and Cargo's package layout (which wraps but does not define today's rule — the rule is `rustc`'s, not Cargo's). The audience crosses from "I author my own module inline with `mod foo { ... }`" (lesson 096) to "I author the same module across two adjacent files with `mod foo;` + `foo.rs`. Same `mod` keyword, same module, same privacy rule — only the body's location changes." This unlocks reading the rmp target's `pub mod bigint;` declaration in `lib.rs` (loading `bigint.rs`, today's file form). The same target's `pub mod biguint;` (loading `biguint/mod.rs`) and every `pub(super)` / `pub(crate)` / `super::` / `crate::` line in `bigint.rs` and `biguint/*.rs` remain blocked downstream and are listed as deferred future moves.
depends_on: 096-inline-module-and-pub (load-bearing — installs `mod foo { ... }` brace form, `pub` on a function, the privacy-by-default rule, and the `foo::item` access form; today extends 096 by *only* the source-layout step. Probe 3 in the evidence appendix witnesses lesson 096's E0603 spanning the file boundary unchanged), 002-fn-main-entry-point (cited — the host `fn main` block in `main.rs`), 008-define-and-call-function (cited — the definition shape `fn name() { ... }` and the call shape `name();` are both unchanged from 008; today moves them across a file boundary), 011-println-positional-args (cited — `println!` with one `{}` slot in the body of `hi`), 043-nested-module-paths (cited — the call form `module::name(args)`; today's `foo::hi()` is that shape, unchanged from 043 and 096), 003-read-rustc-diagnostic (load-bearing — the four-part diagnostic map applied to Probe 2's E0583 transcript; the location underlined is the *declaring* line at `main.rs:1:1`, a different shape from lesson 096's E0603 use-site location, but the four-part structure is identical), 001-rustc-compile-and-run (cited — `rustc main.rs` then `./main`, silent on success), 069-rustc-warnings (cited only — Probe 2's `error: aborting due to 1 previous error` trailer is read with lesson 069's category map), ordinary computer-use (terminal, plain-text editor, `rustc` on `PATH`, Linux/macOS shell, the ability to create *two* files in one directory and run `rustc` from that directory)
unlocks: future "subdirectory modules — `mod foo;` resolving to `foo/mod.rs` when no `foo.rs` is present (Reference items/modules.md lines 82-88); the rmp target uses this with `biguint/mod.rs` to spread one conceptual module across eight files (`add.rs`, `basic.rs`, `cmp.rs`, `convert.rs`, `div.rs`, `format.rs`, `mul.rs`, `shift.rs`); the natural follow-on for today's lesson" moves, future "nested file-based modules — a file-based module body containing its own `mod bar;` lines so `foo.rs` declares another submodule from yet another file; the path-resolution rule for nested file-based modules has its own subtleties per Reference items/modules.md lines 70-88" moves, future "`pub mod foo;` and `pub mod foo { ... }` — making the module declaration itself public; the rmp target's `lib.rs` uses this with `pub mod bigint; pub mod biguint;` to expose its top-level modules to the binary crate via `bignum::bigint::BigInt`; composes today's file-based form with deferred `pub mod` from lesson 096" moves, future "the `#[path = \"...\"]` attribute — overrides the default file-name rule, letting the body live in any file the author chooses; per Reference items/modules.md lines 90-145 (extended discussion of the `path` attribute on inline and outlined modules)" moves, future "the rmp target's first readable `pub mod` lines — `pub mod bigint;` (loads `bigint.rs`, today's form) and `pub mod biguint;` (loads `biguint/mod.rs`, the subdirectory form deferred today); composes today's file-based form with deferred `pub mod`" moves, future "binary + library crate packaging — `lib.rs` exporting modules consumed by `main.rs` via `bignum::bigint::BigInt`; the rmp target's organizational pattern; downstream of today and `pub mod`" moves, future "edition-specific path-resolution differences — the Rust 2015 `mod.rs`-only convention vs. the Rust 2018+ `foo.rs`/`foo/mod.rs` choice; this run uses edition 2024 throughout but the older convention shows up in legacy code" moves, future "Cargo package layout vs `rustc` file rules — Cargo's `src/main.rs`, `src/lib.rs`, `src/foo.rs`, `src/foo/mod.rs` conventions wrap today's `rustc` rule; the conventions are Cargo's, the file-resolution rule itself is `rustc`'s" moves
evidence:
  - output/docs/rust/book/ch07-05-separating-modules-into-different-files.md
  - output/docs/rust/reference/items/modules.md
  - output/docs/rust/error_codes/E0583.md
```
